website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mlb.com">mlb<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Major League Baseball</b> (<b>MLB</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball</a> organization, the oldest of the four <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada</a>. A total of 30 teams play in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) and <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL), with 15 teams in each league. The NL and AL were formed as separate legal entities in 1876 and 1901 respectively. After cooperating but remaining legally separate entities beginning in 1903, the leagues merged into a single organization led by the <a href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_Baseball" title="Commissioner of Baseball">Commissioner of Baseball</a> in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-2000nl_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2000nl-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The organization also oversees <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League Baseball</a>, which comprises 256 teams affiliated with the Major League clubs. With the <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Softball_Confederation" title="World Baseball Softball Confederation">World Baseball Softball Confederation</a>, MLB manages the international <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic" title="World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classic</a> tournament.\n</p><p>Baseball\'s first openly all-professional team was founded in <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a> in 1869. (There had been teams in the past that paid some players, and some that had paid all players but under the table.) The first few decades of professional baseball were characterized by rivalries between leagues and by players who often jumped from one team or league to another. \nThe period before 1920 in baseball was known as the <a href="/wiki/Dead-ball_era" title="Dead-ball era">dead-ball era</a>; players rarely hit <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a> during this time. Baseball survived a conspiracy to <a href="/wiki/Match_fixing" title="Match fixing">fix</a> the <a href="/wiki/1919_World_Series" title="1919 World Series">1919 World Series</a>, which came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sox_Scandal" title="Black Sox Scandal">Black Sox Scandal</a>. The sport rose in popularity in the 1920s, and survived potential downturns during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> and World War II. Shortly after the war, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a> broke <a href="/wiki/Baseball_color_line" title="Baseball color line">baseball\'s color barrier</a>.\n</p><p>The 1950s and 1960s were a time of expansion for the AL and NL, then new stadiums and artificial turf surfaces began to change the game in the 1970s and 1980s. Home runs dominated the game during the 1990s, and media reports began to discuss the use of <a href="/wiki/Anabolic_steroid" title="Anabolic steroid">anabolic steroids</a> among Major League players in the mid-2000s. In 2006, an investigation produced the <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Report" title="Mitchell Report">Mitchell Report</a>, which implicated many players in the use of <a href="/wiki/Performance-enhancing_drugs" class="mw-redirect" title="Performance-enhancing drugs">performance-enhancing substances</a>, including at least one player from each team.\n</p><p>Today, MLB is composed of <a href="/wiki/Current_Major_League_Baseball_franchises" class="mw-redirect" title="Current Major League Baseball franchises">30 teams</a>: 29 in the United States and 1 in Canada. Teams play 162 games each season and five teams in each league advance to a four-round <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_postseason" title="Major League Baseball postseason">postseason tournament</a> that culminates in the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Best-of-seven_playoff" class="mw-redirect" title="Best-of-seven playoff">best-of-seven</a> championship series between the two league champions that dates to 1903. Baseball broadcasts are aired on television, radio, and the Internet throughout North America and in several other countries throughout the world. MLB has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_attendance_figures_at_domestic_professional_sports_leagues" title="List of attendance figures at domestic professional sports leagues">highest season attendance</a> of any sports league in the world with more than 73 million spectators in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizational_structure">Organizational structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Organizational structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>MLB is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Constitution" title="Major League Baseball Constitution">Major League Baseball Constitution</a>. This document has undergone several incarnations since its creation in 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Under the direction of the <a href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_Baseball" title="Commissioner of Baseball">Commissioner of Baseball</a>, MLB hires and maintains the sport\'s <a href="/wiki/Umpire_(baseball)" title="Umpire (baseball)">umpiring</a> crews, and negotiates marketing, labor, and <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_television_contracts" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball television contracts">television contracts</a>. MLB maintains a unique, controlling relationship over the sport, including most aspects of <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League Baseball</a>. This is due in large part to the 1922 <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">U.S. Supreme Court</a> ruling in <i><a href="/wiki/Federal_Baseball_Club_v._National_League" title="Federal Baseball Club v. National League">Federal Baseball Club v. National League</a></i>, which held that baseball is not <a href="/wiki/Commerce_Clause" title="Commerce Clause">interstate commerce</a> and therefore not subject to federal <a href="/wiki/Antitrust" class="mw-redirect" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> law. This ruling has been weakened only slightly in subsequent years.<sup id="cite_ref-Policy_Debate:_Should_the_antitrust_exemption_for_baseball_be_eliminated?_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Policy_Debate:_Should_the_antitrust_exemption_for_baseball_be_eliminated?-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The weakened ruling granted more stability to the owners of teams and has resulted in values increasing at double-digit rates.<sup id="cite_ref-Policy_Debate:_Should_the_antitrust_exemption_for_baseball_be_eliminated?_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Policy_Debate:_Should_the_antitrust_exemption_for_baseball_be_eliminated?-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> There were several challenges to MLB\'s primacy in the sport between the 1870s and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_League" title="Federal League">Federal League</a> in 1916; the last attempt at a new major league was the aborted <a href="/wiki/Continental_League" title="Continental League">Continental League</a> in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-Policy_Debate:_Should_the_antitrust_exemption_for_baseball_be_eliminated?_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Policy_Debate:_Should_the_antitrust_exemption_for_baseball_be_eliminated?-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The chief executive of MLB is the commissioner, currently <a href="/wiki/Rob_Manfred" title="Rob Manfred">Rob Manfred</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chief_operating_officer" title="Chief operating officer">chief operating officer</a> is <a href="/wiki/Tony_Petitti" title="Tony Petitti">Tony Petitti</a>. There are five other executives: president (business and media), chief communications officer, chief legal officer, chief financial officer, and chief baseball officer.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-execs_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-execs-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The multimedia branch of MLB, which is based in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Advanced_Media" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball Advanced Media">MLB Advanced Media</a>. This branch oversees <a href="/wiki/MLB.com" title="MLB.com">MLB.com</a> and each of the 30 teams\' websites. Its charter states that MLB Advanced Media holds <a href="/wiki/Editorial_independence" title="Editorial independence">editorial independence</a> from the league, but it is under the same ownership group and revenue-sharing plan. MLB Productions is a similarly structured wing of the league, focusing on video and traditional broadcast media. MLB also owns 67 percent of <a href="/wiki/MLB_Network" title="MLB Network">MLB Network</a>, with the other 33 percent split between several cable operators and satellite provider <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">DirecTV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It operates out of studios in <a href="/wiki/Secaucus,_New_Jersey" title="Secaucus, New Jersey">Secaucus, New Jersey</a>, and also has editorial independence from the league.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="League_organization">League organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: League organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1920, the weak National Commission, which had been created to manage relationships between the two leagues, was replaced with the much more powerful Commissioner of Baseball, who had the power to make decisions for all of professional baseball unilaterally.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> For 60 years, the American and National Leagues fielded eight teams apiece.\n</p><p>In the 1960s, MLB expansion added eight teams, including the first non-U.S. team (the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a>). Two teams (the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a>) were also added in the 1970s. From 1969 through 1993, each league consisted of an East and West Division. A third division, the Central Division, was added in each league in 1994. Through 1996, the two leagues met on the field only during the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star Game</a>. Regular-season <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague play</a> was introduced in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-Interleague_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interleague-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 1995 two new franchises\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Devil_Rays" class="mw-redirect" title="Tampa Bay Devil Rays">Tampa Bay Devil Rays</a> (now known simply as the Tampa Bay Rays)\xe2\x80\x94were awarded by MLB, to begin play in 1998. This addition brought the total number of franchises to 30. In early 1997, MLB decided to assign one new team to each league: Tampa Bay joined the AL and Arizona joined the NL. The original plan was to have an odd number of teams in each league (15 per league, with 5 in each division). In order for every team to be able to play daily, this would have required interleague play to be scheduled throughout the entire season. However, it was unclear at the time if interleague play would continue after the 1998 season, as it had to be approved by the players\' union. For this and other reasons, it was decided that both leagues should continue to have an even number of teams; one existing club would have to switch leagues. The <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers#1994\xe2\x80\x9398:_Realignment_/_&quot;We&#39;re_taking_this_thing_National&quot;" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> agreed in November 1997 to move from the AL to the NL, thereby making the NL a 16-team league.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Later, when the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> changed ownership prior to the 2013 season, the team moved from the NL Central to the AL West,<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN-AstrosSale2011_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-AstrosSale2011-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ESPN-MLBTeams_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-MLBTeams-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> resulting in both leagues having three divisions of five teams each and allowing all teams to have a more balanced schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN-AstrosSale2011_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-AstrosSale2011-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Interleague play is now held throughout the season.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN-AstrosSale2011_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-AstrosSale2011-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2000 the AL and NL were dissolved as legal entities, and MLB became a single, overall league <i>de jure</i>, similar to the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> (NBA) and <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> (NHL)\xe2\x80\x94albeit with two components called "leagues" instead of "conferences." The same <a href="/wiki/Baseball_rules" title="Baseball rules">rules</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_sport" title="Regulation of sport">regulations</a> are used in both leagues, with one exception: the AL operates under the <a href="/wiki/Designated_hitter" title="Designated hitter">designated hitter</a> rule, while the NL does not.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Anderson_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> This difference in rules between leagues is unique to MLB; the other sports leagues of the U.S. and Canada have one set of rules for all teams.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teams">Teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="img" class="noresize" style="width: 500px;
