\xe2\x80\xa0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>&#160;\n</td>\n<td>1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:pink">\xe2\x80\xa1 <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> (AL)\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>&#160;\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:lightblue">\xe2\x80\xa1 <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> (NL) \xe2\x80\xa0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>&#160;\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4">AL=<a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a><br />NL=<a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4">\xe2\x80\xa0 Totals include a team\'s record in a previous city or under another name<br />(see team article for details).\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4">\xe2\x80\xa1 Have not yet played in a <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4"><small><i>More detail at</i> <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> <i>and</i> <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">List of World Series champions</a><br /><i>Source:</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mlb.mlb.com/mlb/history/postseason/mlb_ws.jsp?feature=club_champs">MLB.com</a></small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>When the regular season ends after the first Sunday in October (or the last Sunday in September), ten teams enter the postseason playoffs. These ten teams consist of six teams that are division champions by earning the best regular season overall <a href="/wiki/Winning_percentage" title="Winning percentage">win-loss record</a> for their respective divisions, and four who are "wild-card" teams that are each one of two teams in their respective leagues who have earned the best regular season win-loss record, but are not division champions. Four rounds of series of games are played to determine the champion:\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Wild_Card_Game" title="Major League Baseball Wild Card Game">Wild Card Game</a>, a one-game playoff between the two wild-card teams in each league.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/American_League_Division_Series" title="American League Division Series">American League Division Series</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_League_Division_Series" title="National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a>, each a best-of-five-games series.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a>, each a best-of-seven-games series played between the winning teams from the Division Series. The league champions are informally referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Pennant_(sports)" title="Pennant (sports)">pennant</a> winners.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>, a best-of-seven-games series played between the pennant winners of each league.</li></ol>\n<p>Within each league, the division winners are the #1, #2 and #3 seeds, based on win\xe2\x80\x93loss records. The team with the best record among non division winners will be the first wildcard and the #4 seed. The team with the second best record among non division winners will be the second wildcard and the #5 seed. In the wildcard round, the #5 seed will play at the #4 seed in a one-game playoff. For the division series, the matchup will be the #1 seed against the Wild Card Game winner and the #2 seed against the #3 seed.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Since 2017, home-field advantage in the World Series is determined by regular-season records of the two league champions, replacing a system used for the prior 14 seasons where the champion of the league that won the All-Star Game would receive home-field advantage.\n</p><p>Because each postseason series is split between the home fields of the two teams, home-field advantage does not usually play a large role in the postseason unless the series goes to its maximum number of games, giving one team an additional game at home. However, the first two games of a postseason series are hosted by the same team. That team may have an increased chance of starting the series with two wins,<sup id="cite_ref-&#91;&#91;World_Series&#93;&#93;_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-[[World_Series]]-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> thereby gaining some momentum for the rest of the series.<sup id="cite_ref-alds_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alds-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The DH rule in the World Series is only used in games played at the American League Champions\' home field. National League home games will play the traditional rules with each teams pitching staff batting.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_play">International play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: International play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/MLB_Japan_All-Star_Series" title="MLB Japan All-Star Series">MLB Japan All-Star Series</a></div>\n<p>Since <a href="/wiki/1986_MLB_Japan_All-Star_Series" title="1986 MLB Japan All-Star Series">1986</a> an <a href="/wiki/All-star_game" title="All-star game">All-Star</a> team from MLB is sent to a biennial end-of-the-season tour of <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, dubbed as <a href="/wiki/MLB_Japan_All-Star_Series" title="MLB Japan All-Star Series">MLB Japan All-Star Series</a>, playing exhibition games in a <a href="/wiki/Playoff_format#Best-of_formats" title="Playoff format">best-of format</a> against the All-Stars from <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Professional_Baseball" title="Nippon Professional Baseball">Nippon Professional Baseball</a> (NPB) or recently as of <a href="/wiki/2014_MLB_Japan_All-Star_Series" title="2014 MLB Japan All-Star Series">2014</a> their national team <a href="/wiki/Samurai_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Samurai Japan">Samurai Japan</a>.\n</p><p>In 2008, MLB played the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_China_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball China Series">MLB China Series</a> in the People\'s Republic of China. It was a series of two spring-training games between the San Diego Padres and Los Angeles Dodgers. The games were an effort to popularize baseball in China.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>MLB played the MLB Taiwan Series in Taiwan in November 2011. It was a series of five exhibition games played by a team made up of MLB players called the MLB All-Stars and the Chinese Taipei National Team. The MLB All-Stars swept the series, five games to zero.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the 2011 season, it was announced that the Seattle Mariners and the Oakland Athletics would play their season openers in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In October 2013, Phil Rogers of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> wrote that MLB was considering postseason all-star tours in Taiwan and Korea; baseball is increasing in popularity in both countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarosh_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarosh-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Arizona Diamondbacks opened the 2014 season against Los Angeles Dodgers on March 22\xe2\x80\x9323 in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The teams played each other at the historic <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground" title="Sydney Cricket Ground">Sydney Cricket Ground</a>, which has a seating capacity of 46,000. The two games represented the first MLB regular-season play held in that country. The games counted as home games for the Diamondbacks, so they played 79 home games at <a href="/wiki/Chase_Field" title="Chase Field">Chase Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Together with the <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Softball_Confederation" title="World Baseball Softball Confederation">World Baseball Softball Confederation</a>, MLB sponsors the <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic" title="World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classic</a>, an international baseball tournament contested by national teams. The Red Sox an Yankees will also play the first ever MLB games in London in the upcoming season.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Steroids_in_baseball">Steroids in baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Steroids in baseball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Doping_in_baseball" title="Doping in baseball">Doping in baseball</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_players_suspended_for_performance-enhancing_drugs" title="List of Major League Baseball players suspended for performance-enhancing drugs">List of Major League Baseball players suspended for performance-enhancing drugs</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmeiro_swing2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Palmeiro_swing2.png/220px-Palmeiro_swing2.png" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Palmeiro_swing2.png/330px-Palmeiro_swing2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Palmeiro_swing2.png/440px-Palmeiro_swing2.png 2x" data-file-width="774" data-file-height="615" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmeiro_swing2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rafael_Palmeiro" title="Rafael Palmeiro">Rafael Palmeiro</a> (batter), one of the MLB players suspended for steroid use<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1998, both <a href="/wiki/Mark_McGwire" title="Mark McGwire">Mark McGwire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Sosa" title="Sammy Sosa">Sammy Sosa</a> hit more than the long-standing single-season MLB record of 61 home runs. <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bonds" title="Barry Bonds">Barry Bonds</a> topped the record in 2001 with 73 home runs. McGwire, Bonds and Sosa became the subjects of speculation regarding the use of performance-enhancing substances. McGwire later admitted that he used a steroid hormone that was still legal in baseball during the 1998 season.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNsteroids_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNsteroids-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Baseball\'s original steroid testing policy, in effect from 2002 to 2005, provided for penalties ranging from a ten-game suspension for a first positive test to a one-year suspension for a fourth positive test. Players were tested at least once per year, with the chance that several players could be tested many times per year.<sup id="cite_ref-wnbc_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wnbc-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 2006 book, <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Shadows" title="Game of Shadows">Game of Shadows</a></i> by <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> investigative reporters <a href="/wiki/Lance_Williams_and_Mark_Fainaru-Wada" title="Lance Williams and Mark Fainaru-Wada">Lance Williams and Mark Fainaru-Wada</a>, chronicled alleged extensive use of performance enhancers, including several types of steroids and <a href="/wiki/Growth_hormone" title="Growth hormone">growth hormone</a> by baseball superstars Barry Bonds, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Sheffield" title="Gary Sheffield">Gary Sheffield</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Giambi" title="Jason Giambi">Jason Giambi</a>. Former <a href="/wiki/Party_leaders_of_the_United_States_Senate" title="Party leaders of the United States Senate">Senate Majority Leader</a> George Mitchell was appointed by Selig on March 30, 2006<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_pre_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB_pre-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> to investigate the use of performance-enhancing drugs in MLB. The appointment was made after several influential members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">U.S. Congress</a> made negative comments about both the effectiveness and honesty of MLB\'s <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_drug_policy" title="Major League Baseball drug policy">drug policies</a> and Commissioner Selig.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_20071213_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_20071213-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The day before the <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Report" title="Mitchell Report">Mitchell Report</a> was to be released in 2007, Selig said, "I haven\'t seen the report yet, but I\'m proud I did it."<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Tribune_20071212_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Tribune_20071212-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-espn_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espn-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The report said that after mandatory random testing began in 2004, <a href="/wiki/Growth_hormone_in_sports" title="Growth hormone in sports">HGH treatment for athletic enhancement</a> became popular among players, as HGH is not detectable in tests. It pointed out that HGH is likely a placebo with no performance-enhancing effects.<sup id="cite_ref-report_pg_SR2_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report_pg_SR2-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The report included substance use allegations against at least one player from each MLB team.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, some people questioned whether Mitchell\'s director role with the Boston Red Sox created a conflict of interest, especially because no "prime [Sox] players were in the report."<sup id="cite_ref-report_pg_A1_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report_pg_A1-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The report named several prominent Yankees who were parts of World Series clubs; there is a long-running and fierce <a href="/wiki/Yankees%E2%80%93Red_Sox_rivalry" title="Yankees\xe2\x80\x93Red Sox rivalry">Yankees\xe2\x80\x93Red Sox rivalry</a>. Former U.S. prosecutor <a href="/wiki/John_M._Dowd" title="John M. Dowd">John M. Dowd</a> brought up Mitchell\'s conflict of interest,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> but he later said that the former senator had done a good job.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Mitchell acknowledged that his "tight relationship with Major League Baseball left him open to criticism",<sup id="cite_ref-gregjohnson_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gregjohnson-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> but he said that readers who examine the report closely "will not find any evidence of bias, of special treatment of the Red Sox".<sup id="cite_ref-gregjohnson_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gregjohnson-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On January 10, 2013, MLB and the players union reached an agreement to add random, in-season HGH testing. They also agreed to implement a new test to reveal the use of <a href="/wiki/Testosterone_(medication)" title="Testosterone (medication)">testosterone</a> for the 2013 season.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The current MLB drug policy provides for an 80-game suspension for a first positive test, a 162-game suspension for a second positive test, and a lifetime suspension for a third positive test.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, allegations surfaced against <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Ortiz" title="David Ortiz">David Ortiz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manny_Ramirez" title="Manny Ramirez">Manny Ramirez</a> received a 50-game suspension after testing positive for banned substances. In early April 2011, Ramirez retired from baseball rather than face a 100-game suspension for his second positive steroid test.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> He would later unretire, having the suspension dropped to 50 games, and would serve those in 2012.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_television" title="Major League Baseball on television">Major League Baseball on television</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_Major_League_Baseball_broadcasters" title="List of current Major League Baseball broadcasters">List of current Major League Baseball broadcasters</a></div>\n<p>Several networks televise baseball games, including <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_(United_States)" title="Fox Sports (United States)">Fox</a>, ESPN, and MLB Network. Since 2008, Fox Sports has broadcast MLB games on <i><a href="/wiki/Fox_Major_League_Baseball" title="Fox Major League Baseball">Fox Saturday Baseball</a></i> throughout the entire season; Fox previously only broadcast games from May to September.<sup id="cite_ref-fox_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fox-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Fox also holds rights to the All-Star Game each season. Fox also alternates League Championship Series broadcasts, broadcasting the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> (ALCS) in odd-numbered years and the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a> (NLCS) in even-numbered years. Fox broadcasts all games of the World Series. ESPN continues to broadcast MLB games through 2013 as well, beginning with national Opening Day coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> ESPN broadcasts <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Night_Baseball" title="Sunday Night Baseball">Sunday Night Baseball</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Monday_Night_Baseball" title="Monday Night Baseball">Monday Night Baseball</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Wednesday_Night_Baseball" title="Wednesday Night Baseball">Wednesday Night Baseball</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Baseball_Tonight" title="Baseball Tonight">Baseball Tonight</a></i>. ESPN also has rights to the <a href="/wiki/Home_Run_Derby" title="Home Run Derby">Home Run Derby</a> at the All-Star Game each July.<sup id="cite_ref-espn_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espn-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/TBS_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="TBS (TV network)">TBS</a> airs <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_TBS" title="Major League Baseball on TBS">Sunday afternoon regular season games</a> (non-exclusive) nationally. In 2007, TBS began its exclusive rights to any tiebreaker games that determine division or wild card champions; it also airs exclusive coverage of the <a href="/wiki/Division_Series" title="Division Series">Division Series</a> round of the playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-tbs_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbs-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> TBS carries the <a href="/wiki/League_Championship_Series" title="League Championship Series">League Championship Series</a> that are not included under Fox\'s television agreement; TBS shows the NLCS in odd-numbered years and the ALCS in even-numbered years.<sup id="cite_ref-tv_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tv-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2009, MLB launched the MLB Network, featuring news and coverage from around the league, and airing 26 live games in the 2009 season.<sup id="cite_ref-washpost_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washpost-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Each team also has local broadcasts for all games not carried by Fox on Saturdays or ESPN on Sunday nights. These games are typically split between a local broadcast television station and a local or <a href="/wiki/Regional_sports_network" title="Regional sports network">regional sports network</a> (RSN), though some teams only air local games through RSNs or through their own team networks. As Canada only contains one team, <a href="/wiki/Sportsnet" title="Sportsnet">Sportsnet</a> broadcasts Toronto Blue Jays games nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-Sportsnet_will_carry_all_162_games_for_Blue_Jays_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sportsnet_will_carry_all_162_games_for_Blue_Jays-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The channel is owned by <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Communications" title="Rogers Communications">Rogers Communications</a>, who is also the parent company of the Blue Jays.<sup id="cite_ref-Sportsnet_will_carry_all_162_games_for_Blue_Jays_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sportsnet_will_carry_all_162_games_for_Blue_Jays-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Sportsnet also televises Fox\'s Saturday afternoon games, the All-Star Game, playoff games, and the World Series.<sup id="cite_ref-Sportsnet_will_carry_all_162_games_for_Blue_Jays_163-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sportsnet_will_carry_all_162_games_for_Blue_Jays-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sportsnet_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sportsnet-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> In April 2011, <a href="/wiki/TSN2" title="TSN2">TSN2</a> began carrying ESPN <i>Sunday Night Baseball</i> in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-TSN2_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TSN2-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blackout_policy">Blackout policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Blackout policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_blackout_policy" title="Major League Baseball blackout policy">Major League Baseball blackout policy</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Syndication_exclusivity" title="Syndication exclusivity">Syndication exclusivity</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MLB_Blackout_Areas.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/MLB_Blackout_Areas.png/300px-MLB_Blackout_Areas.png" width="300" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/MLB_Blackout_Areas.png/450px-MLB_Blackout_Areas.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/MLB_Blackout_Areas.png/600px-MLB_Blackout_Areas.png 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MLB_Blackout_Areas.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>MLB blackout map in the United States</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canadian_MLB_Blackout_map.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Canadian_MLB_Blackout_map.PNG/300px-Canadian_MLB_Blackout_map.PNG" width="300" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Canadian_MLB_Blackout_map.PNG/450px-Canadian_MLB_Blackout_map.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Canadian_MLB_Blackout_map.PNG/600px-Canadian_MLB_Blackout_map.PNG 2x" data-file-width="707" data-file-height="432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canadian_MLB_Blackout_map.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Canadian MLB blackout map</div></div></div>\n<p>MLB has several <a href="/wiki/Blackout_(broadcasting)" title="Blackout (broadcasting)">blackout</a> rules.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> A local broadcaster has priority to televise games of the team in their market over national broadcasters. For example, at one time TBS showed many Atlanta Braves games nationally and internationally in Canada. <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Networks" title="Fox Sports Networks">Fox Sports Networks</a> also show many games in other areas. If the Braves played a team that FSN or another local broadcaster showed, the local station will have the broadcast rights for its own local market, while TBS would have been blacked out in the same market during the game. A market that has a local team playing in a weekday ESPN or <a href="/wiki/ESPN2" title="ESPN2">ESPN2</a> game and is shown on a local station will see <a href="/wiki/ESPNews" title="ESPNews">ESPNews</a>, or, in the past, another game scheduled on ESPN or ESPN2 at the same time (if ESPN or ESPN2 operates a regional coverage broadcasting and operates a game choice), or will be subject to an alternative programming feed.<sup id="cite_ref-Helyar_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Helyar-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> MLB\'s streaming Internet video service is also subject to the same blackout rules.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_Internet">Radio and Internet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Radio and Internet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_the_radio" title="Major League Baseball on the radio">Major League Baseball on the radio</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/ESPN_Radio" title="ESPN Radio">ESPN Radio</a> holds national broadcast rights and broadcasts <i>Sunday Night Baseball</i> weekly throughout the season in addition to all playoff games.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The rights to the World Series are exclusive to ESPN.\n</p><p>In addition, each team employs its own announcers, who broadcast during the regular season. Most teams operate regional networks to cover their fan bases; some of these supposedly regional networks (such as the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees_Radio_Network" title="New York Yankees Radio Network">New York Yankees Radio Network</a>) have a national reach with affiliates located across the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Major League Baseball has an exclusive rights deal with <a href="/wiki/XM_Satellite_Radio" title="XM Satellite Radio">XM Satellite Radio</a>, which includes the channel <a href="/wiki/MLB_Network_Radio" title="MLB Network Radio">MLB Network Radio</a> and live play-by-play of all games.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Many teams also maintain a network of stations that broadcast their games in Spanish; the former <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a> broadcast their games in both English and French.\n</p><p>MLB games are also broadcast live on the internet. All television and radio broadcasts of games are available via subscription to <a href="/wiki/MLB.tv" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB.tv">MLB.tv</a> at Major League Baseball\'s website, MLB.com, and radio-only broadcasts are also available via subscription to MLB.com Gameday Audio.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Radio station affiliates are officially forbidden from streaming games through their Internet feeds. Blackout rules are still applied for live television broadcasts, but not radio broadcasts.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_broadcasting">International broadcasting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: International broadcasting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/ESPN_Deportes" title="ESPN Deportes">ESPN Deportes</a> televises a large number of MLB games in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Language">Spanish</a> throughout Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-deportes_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deportes-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WAPA-TV" title="WAPA-TV">Wapa 2</a> airs games in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, including spring training games and most of the World Baseball Classic games involving the team from Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-PH_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> In Brazil, <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Brasil" title="ESPN Brasil">ESPN Brasil</a> has exclusive rights on TV (<a href="/wiki/ESPN_Latin_America" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPN Latin America">ESPN</a> and ESPN+) and Internet (<a href="/wiki/WatchESPN" title="WatchESPN">WatchESPN</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports" title="Fox Sports">Fox Sports</a> also broadcasting some games.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Channel_5_(UK)" title="Channel 5 (UK)">Five</a> in the United Kingdom previously screened MLB games, including the All-Star Game and the <a href="/wiki/Mlb#Postseason" class="mw-redirect" title="Mlb">postseason</a> games, on Sunday and Wednesday usually starting at 1&#160;a.m. <a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">BST</a>. Most recently, <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Gould" class="mw-redirect" title="Johnny Gould">Johnny Gould</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Chetwynd" title="Josh Chetwynd">Josh Chetwynd</a> presented <i><a href="/wiki/MLB_on_Five" title="MLB on Five">MLB on Five</a></i> on that station.<sup id="cite_ref-five_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-five-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The channel covered baseball beginning on its opening night in 1997, but for financial reasons, the decision was made not to pick up MLB for the 2009 season.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPN UK">ESPN UK</a> show live and recorded games several times a week\xe2\x80\x94it is available with <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a> and (on a subscriber-basis) <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media#Virgin_TV" title="Virgin Media">Virgin Media</a> in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN_America" title="ESPN America">ESPN America</a> televised a large number of games in the UK and dozens of other countries; in May 2013, ESPN announced that it would shut down the channel on July 31, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Spy_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spy-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Suspend_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suspend-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Australia, MLB games are regularly shown on <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Australia" title="ESPN Australia">ESPN Australia</a> (subscription).<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the Middle East &amp; North Africa, MLB games are broadcast on <a href="/wiki/BeIN_Sports_Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="BeIN Sports Arabia">beIN Sports</a> channels.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
